<span id="freeTextContainer4588690882535368312">DUMA KEY had so much promise.... GREAT story in the beginning. Then when Edgar Freemantle and Wireman got together, the direction and dialogue just became silly. I don't know of any 2 grown men who converse in the same way as Edgar and Wireman did. It was forced and overly trite. That was the beginning of the end for me. I was also disgusted with how King wraps everything up in Florida. Hard to buy into it all. DUMA KEY was ultimately a big disappointment.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_839714230" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/839714230" />
    <a title="Sadie Hartmann Mother Horror" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28225370-sadie-hartmann-mother-horror"><img alt="Sadie Hartmann Mother Horror" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596596514p2/28225370.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/839714230?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sadie Hartmann Mother Horror" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sadie Hartmann Mother Horror" href="/user/show/28225370-sadie-hartmann-mother-horror">Sadie Hartmann Mother Horror</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer839714230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12955101102107901008">It's been years since I first read Duma Key. While I loved it the first time around and gave a five star rating, it's possible I loved it more the second time around. <br/>I think just knowing the story better and where it was going, helped clarify some of the more supernatural aspects of certain events early on.<br/>Lately, (on bookstagram) I've seen people rating a King book lower *because* he had a supernatural element to an otherwise, genre specific story--example: The Outsider. People thought it shou</span>
  <span id="freeText12955101102107901008" style="display:none">It's been years since I first read Duma Key. While I loved it the first time around and gave a five star rating, it's possible I loved it more the second time around. <br />I think just knowing the story better and where it was going, helped clarify some of the more supernatural aspects of certain events early on.<br />Lately, (on bookstagram) I've seen people rating a King book lower *because* he had a supernatural element to an otherwise, genre specific story--example: The Outsider. People thought it should have just been a detective novel.<br />Well, let me step up on this platform as a seasoned Constant Reader for second and announce that Mr. King is well known and admired for his genre-bending stories. The Dark Tower series, for instance, is everything. It's a Western, dark fantasy, horror, supernatural, apocalyptic, science fiction/time travel, you name it, it's probably in there to some degree.<br />Duma Key is not going to be pigeon-holed into a genre either so be prepared to just enjoy the ride and not try to figure it out--at its core, this story is about a man who has had his life stripped away after a body (and soul crushing) accident on the job.<br />He goes to Florida to stay in a big house at the edge of the sea for some contemplative walks on the beach. Of course this is a King novel so Edgar Freemantle isn't going to be left alone at "Big Pink" despite however lonely he feels, right?<br />Right.<br />My favorite aspect to this novel are the relationships. The unexpected deep friendship between Wireman and Edgar and perhaps even the crazy love between Fathers and Daughters, even the destructive/toxic relationship between former lovers is intense and compelling--told through dialog and inner mind chat that only King can tell it.<br />The climax and the way the story takes on that snowball-racing-down-an-avalanche feeling towards the end is some of King's best work.<br />This is definitely a top 20 if not top 10 King ranking for me.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12955101102107901008" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1084118558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1084118558" />
    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1084118558?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Daviau" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau">Ashley Daviau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1084118558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8603351045582102888">It’s been years since I first read this book and I loved it even more this time around which I didn’t think was possible. In fact, I consider it one of my top 5 King books now! I think it’s one of those books that gets better every time you read it, you catch a little something new each time. This time around it struck me so profoundly, I felt like I was sucked into the book and I was living the story alongside Edgar and Wireman. It was such a beautiful and yet terrifying feeling, being so entra</span>
  <span id="freeText8603351045582102888" style="display:none">It’s been years since I first read this book and I loved it even more this time around which I didn’t think was possible. In fact, I consider it one of my top 5 King books now! I think it’s one of those books that gets better every time you read it, you catch a little something new each time. This time around it struck me so profoundly, I felt like I was sucked into the book and I was living the story alongside Edgar and Wireman. It was such a beautiful and yet terrifying feeling, being so entranced and hypnotized by a story and its characters. Especially since this story does get quite scary at some points, it literally had chills going down my back and had me jumping at every sound I heard in the dark while I was reading it. I could go on and on about how much I loved my reread of Duma Key but I’ll leave it at that before I bore you all!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8603351045582102888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_98614298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98614298" />
    <a title="Kasia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2087548-kasia"><img alt="Kasia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494441972p2/2087548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98614298?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kasia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kasia" href="/user/show/2087548-kasia">Kasia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98614298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4220095568428098392">Ahh... what can I say about Duma Key, other than it being an extraordinary experience, a literary breath of fresh air, a masterpiece of color and texture without any actual paint being used. I guess there are some people out there think it's boring or long but I instantaneously felt a bond with the book and I can say that I absolutely loved it! The writing itself was so colorful and interesting that I enjoyed each and every page, there was in no rush to get to the ending by any means, but I did </span>
  <span id="freeText4220095568428098392" style="display:none">Ahh... what can I say about Duma Key, other than it being an extraordinary experience, a literary breath of fresh air, a masterpiece of color and texture without any actual paint being used. I guess there are some people out there think it's boring or long but I instantaneously felt a bond with the book and I can say that I absolutely loved it! The writing itself was so colorful and interesting that I enjoyed each and every page, there was in no rush to get to the ending by any means, but I did like the end, it matched the enigmatic feel of the story and it had a lush, tropical feel to it but it was tainted by something dark and eerie and quite frankly very creepy because it was deadly. Those affected could have never imagine their demise, and whether they believed in it or not, it was coming. I was attracted to this book right away, partially because of the cover; it always begged to be read and as an artist it touched my sensors in ways that kept me thinking of it often so I finally had to sit down and read it and also because one of my best friends started reading it and I had to follow suit so we could enjoy and discuss it together, it was a real treat to read it at the same time and marvel at the unfolding story. <br /><br />Edgar Freemantle is a handicapped man who moves to a mythical island of Duma Key, a place that doesn't exist in reality but seems more real than half the vacation spots I've been in. He rents a salmon colored house and starts painting with his remaining arm, paintings that change his life - at first for the better but later he realizes that his new found gift is very hungry, and it hungers for things most precious to him. His recovery seems to progress until he starts feeling his missing arm, at the same time strange storms are coming to the island and things that shouldn't be real are happening, Edgar knows that his paintings have more power and meaning than he could have ever imagined and it's up to him to solve the mystery that has enshrouded Duma Key for generations and left many skeletons during it's rein. The story jumps off the cliff with an appearance of a ship on the horizon, Edgar knows that its not good news, something strange and deadly is on that ship and the closer it gets to him during those storms the stranger the hold on his sudden artistic talents and the results are quite shocking, but hey they make for great reading. After reading it I can safely say that it's one of my favorite books ever, I even got the hard cover version so I could have the full dust jacket with it's glorious art to see while I read the paperback and carried it with me everywhere. This might not be for everyone, but that's totally fine with me, I loved it and it made an impact on me, I'm sure there are people out there who wont like it, and that's fine, It only makes me feel lucky that I'm not one of them! <br /><br />This story is like an exotic fruit bowl, gorgeous from every angle and full of mouth watering rainbow of flavors. The characters in this tale are extremely realistic, from the kooky and zany to mysterious and deadly, each plays a part that paints such a grand picture that the more I think about it the more I feel the need to read it again, just to dip back into that pool of "ahh.." it creates.. It's really hard to explain but this book was marvelous and it made a bond with my imagination, one that will stay with me for a long time. There is plenty of original mystery and horror and love and growth combined with struggles and some deaths, it all paints a picture worth thousands of words, one that I could stare at forever.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4220095568428098392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1002654181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1002654181" />
    <a title="Gary " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27528763-gary"><img alt="Gary " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499717454p2/27528763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1002654181?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary " href="/user/show/27528763-gary">Gary </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27528763-gary?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27528763-gary?shelf=classic-lit">classic-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1002654181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9376557448973000161">This book is a return to King in his classic style. The writing was tight and concise, umlike some of his 90s material which tended to ramble a bit. He claims to be writing more slowly as he ages, and tyhis is working in his favor. This book capitalizes on the author’s ability to create likable characters that we care about, foreshadow tragedy, and establish settings that can drive the story when the plot lags.<br/>The story focuses on Edgar, a protagonist that has suffered a tragedy and goes to an i</span>
  <span id="freeText9376557448973000161" style="display:none">This book is a return to King in his classic style. The writing was tight and concise, umlike some of his 90s material which tended to ramble a bit. He claims to be writing more slowly as he ages, and tyhis is working in his favor. This book capitalizes on the author’s ability to create likable characters that we care about, foreshadow tragedy, and establish settings that can drive the story when the plot lags.<br />The story focuses on Edgar, a protagonist that has suffered a tragedy and goes to an island off the coast of Florida to recuperate. The island, of course, is not the relaxing vacation which it first appears to be. The setting comes to life through the author’s trade mark variety of techniques that apply to the five senses. Seashells scrape beneath the house like skeleton bones; the island appears deserted except, of course, for one old woman at the other end of it.<br />Anyone that has a daughter or is a daughter will relate to Illy, the protagonist’s daughter. Marriage, tragedy and familial relations weave into the pot until they become an integral part of the story even for hardened horror buffs. Even the supporting characters (including the late introduced ones) quickly appear round and lifelike.<br />Reading this book reminds me that we are in the presence of a modern master that will be studied for many years to come. He is already appearing in literature textbooks in our classrooms. As I spent my late July nights turning these pages, I was reminded of college days spent reading this author’s novels unable to put them down. <br />There were parts of the story that slowed down, particularly in the center of the storyline. At times I took breaks and returned to this and with a little patience my attention was hooked again. The author’s talent carries a lagging story when it has to. Soon enough the story hooked me into its momentum quickly enough and the story wraps in a fashion that only a master storyteller can do, building crescendo as it climbs. Many of this author’s novels in the 80s and 90s began to read like the movie was already in his mind when he was writing. This book reads like a writer that is in the late years of his career and is enjoying the talent he has been given.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9376557448973000161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1883183308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1883183308" />
    <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf"><img alt="Cody | CodysBookshelf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592500568p2/56352820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1883183308?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody | CodysBookshelf" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf">Cody | CodysBookshelf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=halloween-bingo-2019">halloween-bingo-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883183308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8117833641909000780"><b>2019 Update:</b><br/>A novel that grows in my estimation upon each reread, it has now earned a spot in my top 3. Hell, it could be my favorite King novel. SK writes about the creative process with clarity, and his setting of a ghost-ridden, Gothic-esque island in south Florida is one of his most invigorating and unsettling. Pair that with outright poetic prose and some of this author’s scariest sequences, and you have a bonafide winner.<br/><br/><b>Read for ‘600+ pages’ in Halloween Bingo.</b><br/><br/><b>Original Review:</b><br/><br/>What can I s</span>
  <span id="freeText8117833641909000780" style="display:none"><b>2019 Update:</b><br />A novel that grows in my estimation upon each reread, it has now earned a spot in my top 3. Hell, it could be my favorite King novel. SK writes about the creative process with clarity, and his setting of a ghost-ridden, Gothic-esque island in south Florida is one of his most invigorating and unsettling. Pair that with outright poetic prose and some of this author’s scariest sequences, and you have a bonafide winner.<br /><br /><b>Read for ‘600+ pages’ in Halloween Bingo.</b><br /><br /><b>Original Review:</b><br /><br />What can I say about this novel that has not already been said thousands of times over in the last ten years? That it is a watertight, late-era Stephen King masterpiece? That it is a mature and pensive rumination on loss and memory? That it is easily as unsettling as iconic King works such as <i>Pet Sematary</i> and <i>The Shining</i>? All those would be true, yes, but would it be redundant? I mean, you know all this, don’t you?<br /><br />Maybe you don’t.<br /><br />For whatever reason — mayhap it is ka — this 2008 novel continues to fly under the radar. Maybe because it is sandwiched between the divisive <i>Lisey’s Story</i> and the gargantuan <i>Under the Dome</i>. Maybe because it picks and reworks themes from past King works (the psi powers a’la <i>The Dead Zone</i>, a climatic scene set in a well that bears a passing resemblance to <i>Dolores Claiborne</i>), and maybe readers felt, consciously or subconsciously, King was running out of steam when this novel released. I don’t know; I was not aware of this man or his works in 2008. This just seems to be the general consensus: <i>Duma Key</i> is a forgettable, mixed bag.<br /><br />Oh, but it isn’t true. In fact, it is one of King’s very best.<br /><br />This novel feels unique for this author due to two things: the setting (the Florida Keys), and the main character’s wild artistic talent. Some of King’s very best writing reflects the artistic process itself; nowhere is that more clear than in this story, as the reader witnesses Edgar Freemantle overcome a crippling accident and an explosive divorce by almost literally drawing himself back into the world. <br /><br />A modern masterpiece, this title does not get the praise it deserves, and that’s a shame. My highest recommendation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8117833641909000780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1459157195" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1459157195" />
    <a title="Wayne Barrett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21372390-wayne-barrett"><img alt="Wayne Barrett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601067617p2/21372390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1459157195?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wayne Barrett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wayne Barrett" href="/user/show/21372390-wayne-barrett">Wayne Barrett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=paranormal-ghosts">paranormal-ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1459157195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9112217013129695182"><br/>I'll have to mirror fellow reviewer and friend, Edward Lorn on this one because, as he pointed out, this novel did strike me as a mix between Pet Cemetery and Bag of Bones.<br/><br/>King did a great job with the character development and plot line. Unlike Bag of Bones, which felt a little weak for me, Duma Key was laid down with great depth and power. If I had a complaint, and what keeps me from giving it 5 stars, is that after following this deep drama for so long, the climax seemed a little silly in con</span>
  <span id="freeText9112217013129695182" style="display:none"><br />I'll have to mirror fellow reviewer and friend, Edward Lorn on this one because, as he pointed out, this novel did strike me as a mix between Pet Cemetery and Bag of Bones.<br /><br />King did a great job with the character development and plot line. Unlike Bag of Bones, which felt a little weak for me, Duma Key was laid down with great depth and power. If I had a complaint, and what keeps me from giving it 5 stars, is that after following this deep drama for so long, the climax seemed a little silly in context to the build up. It still wasn't bad and overall this was a good King novel. </span>

<div id="review_3423042076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3423042076" />
    <a title="Gary K Bibliophile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92857550-gary-k-bibliophile"><img alt="Gary K Bibliophile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554731392p2/92857550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3423042076?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary K Bibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary K Bibliophile" href="/user/show/92857550-gary-k-bibliophile">Gary K Bibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3423042076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11724419998536441328">“I can do this” - A recurring inspirational thought of Edgar Freemantle (no relation to Abigail... or are they? 🤔 ) during his long recovery from a near fatal worksite accident. The accident cost him his arm and badly injured his legs, caused lingering memory and speech issues, and ultimately broke up his marriage. It also provided him with financial means to escape from it all and relocate to Duma Key FL to aid in his rehabilitation. <br/><br/>Part of his recovery included a reconnection with his persona</span>
  <span id="freeText11724419998536441328" style="display:none">“I can do this” - A recurring inspirational thought of Edgar Freemantle (no relation to Abigail... or are they? 🤔 ) during his long recovery from a near fatal worksite accident. The accident cost him his arm and badly injured his legs, caused lingering memory and speech issues, and ultimately broke up his marriage. It also provided him with financial means to escape from it all and relocate to Duma Key FL to aid in his rehabilitation. <br /><br />Part of his recovery included a reconnection with his personal interests in art. He never considered himself a great artist and decided as a career to provide for his family via more traditional means. After the accident, his therapist suggested he start it up again since it was something he enjoyed... Of course this is the same therapist that thought ‘Reba the anger management doll’ (Edgar named it Reba) was a good idea... so not all of his ideas are the best. <br /><br />Ok... so that’s about as much of the plot as I’m willing to divulge - I don’t want to give away too much. I will say that this is kind of SK’s demented take on ‘Harold and the Purple Crayon’ - Maybe Beryl Evans could offer up an additional story to that series??<br /><br />The characters in this book - while flawed - are very likable. The main character - Edgar - struggles a lot from his speech, memory, and anger issues. You really feel for him and want him to succeed. I also personally want to nominate Jerome Wireman on a short list of ‘best supporting character to appear in a SK novel’. He is a good friend to Edgar and an overall good person. Also, I always make a point to note when SK makes a mention of Nebraska (where I live)... and in this case Wireman is a former lawyer from Omaha. In one part there is mention of Edgar and Jerome having a ‘palaver’... a wonderful Dark Tower reference. Additionally, Jerome cares for an elderly woman named Elizabeth Eastlake. The three of them seem to be drawn together (see what I did there?) for a reason.<br /><br />There are lots of interesting SK bits thrown in... Rock-n-Roll references galore and a subtle nod to classic Saturday Night Live’s “Cheeseburger Cheeseburger” sketch. Over the course of the book you learn ‘How to Draw a Picture’. Catch phrases like “Maybe sí maybe no” and “You nasty man” recur throughout. I learned what a Ha-Ha’ was (it’s a type of wall). Also, a Heart Shaped Box made an appearance... a year after his son Joe Hill published a book of the same name. <br /><br />As you would expect in an SK story there are a lot of dark elements too. Many dark themes and individual backstories, twisted animals, demented dolls (yes... multiple), and things from the deep that reminded me of Creepshow. I also liked the spookiness of ‘abyssus abyssum invocat’ - Hell invokes Hell.<br /><br />Since there was no movie on this one (yet - it’s marked in-production) and the title didn’t give much away... I didn’t know what to expect going into this one. I was very pleasantly surprised and very much recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11724419998536441328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_21172049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21172049" />
    <a title="Imogen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33887-imogen"><img alt="Imogen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353870889p2/33887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21172049?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Imogen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Imogen" href="/user/show/33887-imogen">Imogen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21172049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2591364090829835288">More literal magical negros than we usually mean when we use that phrase (although this one shows teaches white people things too), more classic-rock-oriented tragic heroes than you see in Sophocles, and arche/stereotypes so predictable and effective that you're totally sucked in even as you're laughing at the dialogue and the plot twists: you know when you are reading Stephen King. <br/><br/>I'm glad I started reading him when I was little and I liked everything, instead of now that I am old and I hate e</span>
  <span id="freeText2591364090829835288" style="display:none">More literal magical negros than we usually mean when we use that phrase (although this one shows teaches white people things too), more classic-rock-oriented tragic heroes than you see in Sophocles, and arche/stereotypes so predictable and effective that you're totally sucked in even as you're laughing at the dialogue and the plot twists: you know when you are reading Stephen King. <br /><br />I'm glad I started reading him when I was little and I liked everything, instead of now that I am old and I hate everything, because I can't imagine how this stuff would read if it weren't so familiar that it's comforting. The plot is pretty much irrelevent, you know? Monster dolls, eh. Also, you know the thing where sometimes boys treat their girlfriends like shit but they think it's okay because they're like, "Man, she is smarter and better than me," and their words are supposed to make their behavior okay? Ol' Steve is like that but not to his girlfriend- to black people. <br /><br />Still, pretty much everybody comes off douchey, and Steve can't ever seem to resist throwing in stuff about bands he likes (all dorky 70s rock and, I think, maybe Shark Puppy is actually his own band?) like a first-year creative writing student, which feel so transparently self-indulgent. <br /><br />So... yeah. Dunno why I read six hundred pages of this stuff and enjoyed it, except that it makes me feel like little eleven-year-old me reading a library copy of the Stand while the other kids are playing little league, thinking 'MAN BOOKS ARE AWESOME.'</span>
  <a data-text-id="2591364090829835288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2159587243122063353">4.5 rounded up. I’m really surprised this isn’t more talked about because it’s really very good. As with any King book you care to pick up, you feel like you know the main characters because he takes the time to go to town on the small details, the thought processes, the motivations, wants, desires and needs. The setting here is a little different-not a small town, rather a small island. It is an atmospheric and creepy read in places. The positive vibes on setting up on the island soon turn sini</span>
  <span id="freeText2159587243122063353" style="display:none">4.5 rounded up. I’m really surprised this isn’t more talked about because it’s really very good. As with any King book you care to pick up, you feel like you know the main characters because he takes the time to go to town on the small details, the thought processes, the motivations, wants, desires and needs. The setting here is a little different-not a small town, rather a small island. It is an atmospheric and creepy read in places. The positive vibes on setting up on the island soon turn sinister though.</span>

<div id="review_1746506991" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1746506991" />
    <a title="Rafael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21797839-rafael"><img alt="Rafael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530497034p2/21797839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1746506991?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rafael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rafael" href="/user/show/21797839-rafael">Rafael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1746506991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1923830806634631377">This particular Stephen king book is a poem to art, being a designer and art enthusiast this book hit me on the spot. <br/><br/>Wealthy construction contractor Edgar Freemantle recently a survivor of a crane accident that left him with a bad hip, only one arm, a terrible memory and very bad case of anger, that led to a divorce with his wife, has decided he's had enough and wishes to start a new life away from what he knows in to a new environment, that is when he finds Duma Key, a beach paradise with a Bi</span>
  <span id="freeText1923830806634631377" style="display:none">This particular Stephen king book is a poem to art, being a designer and art enthusiast this book hit me on the spot. <br /><br />Wealthy construction contractor Edgar Freemantle recently a survivor of a crane accident that left him with a bad hip, only one arm, a terrible memory and very bad case of anger, that led to a divorce with his wife, has decided he's had enough and wishes to start a new life away from what he knows in to a new environment, that is when he finds Duma Key, a beach paradise with a Big pink house just for him, the solitude, the view and the sounds of the ocean inspire him to move more, walk, rehabilitate for himself and oddly paint, like he did long ago but this time felt different, the beach takes him to a life-changing chain of events, he finds new friendships, like Jerome Wireman and jack cantori, he finds talent, a new life like he wanted but all with a price and a reason! <br /><br />This Book took me a long time to read, honestly, don't know why, I guess I did not want it to end, felt like a personal journey, it's a big book but not massive, but the story and the characters deeply connects and sink in to you, like it was your own personal experience, I can not stop thinking of this story, and often find myself wondering around Big Pink on my mind, listening to the shells.<br /><br />So if you're in for a journey this is your book ”Muchacho” come on let's go to Duma key, who knows? Maybe you'll feel like you just won ”la Loteria”</span>
  <a data-text-id="1923830806634631377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CuEmi+lCMGV9oYyi2v79gB97vRs5d/gCyhVGS9a5F911VcJpaMjKt8BaIf+ZPhKoSYnkcVYLT570Jz6RUd37ug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1dWGgXXN5GPv3HBAK0YVgmh3ONrj7eRpuSkntnXh2NKqYWJj9EcesVIn3R1ohvqqPoVhsIyRU/WHG19s8oU0tQ==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
750,395
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7038656662641474665">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText7038656662641474665" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7038656662641474665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
